  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1101050671?book_show_action=true">Nov 08, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="BookLover" class="user" itemprop="url" name="BookLover" href="/user/show/12285159-booklover">BookLover</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12285159-booklover?shelf=tpl">tpl</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12285159-booklover?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12285159-booklover?shelf=reviews">reviews</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12285159-booklover?shelf=rs">rs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12285159-booklover?shelf=paperback">paperback</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12285159-booklover?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12285159-booklover?shelf=audio">audio</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1101050671" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11145767080168358282"><i>Re-read in 2017 - sigh, nothing new to add here, except, this book gets better and better with each read</i><br/><br/><i>Re-read in 2016 - this book, an all-time favourite, was just what I needed this week!!! Loved it just as much this time around. Every word was perfection. sigh!</i><br/><br/>**Original review 04/24/15**<br/>Oh, my poor heart, how I loved this book. How is it possible that Rainbow Rowell, no matter who the character is, no matter what the storyline, can get inside and make me feel every minute of her stories? Wha</span>
  <span id="freeText11145767080168358282" style="display:none"><i>Re-read in 2017 - sigh, nothing new to add here, except, this book gets better and better with each read</i><br /><br /><i>Re-read in 2016 - this book, an all-time favourite, was just what I needed this week!!! Loved it just as much this time around. Every word was perfection. sigh!</i><br /><br />**Original review 04/24/15**<br />Oh, my poor heart, how I loved this book. How is it possible that Rainbow Rowell, no matter who the character is, no matter what the storyline, can get inside and make me feel every minute of her stories? What a fantastic storyteller!<br /><br />This was such a unique story, told in a unique way. Throughout the story, we get to read email correspondence between best friends Beth and Jennifer as well as read all about Lincoln, the IT guy hired to read company emails flagged for inappropriate use. <br /><br />It was set in 1999/2000, which totally brought me back to that time in my life. I, too, was working for a newspaper around that time and email was a relatively new thing in the workplace. I think I would have died of embarrassment if anyone had been reading any of the emails send back and forth between my friends and I during that time. How naive we were back then with no concept of big brother and the digital trail left behind with our correspondence.<br /><br />This was a sweet story with great characters. <br /><br />I was able to get a real picture of who Beth and Jennifer were through their emails. Their friendship was funny and heartwarming.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>“Beth to Jennifer - My Cute Guy has a kid.<br />Can you believe it? A kid! And probably a wife, too. How could he do this to me?<br />Jennifer to Beth- ???<br />Beth to Jennifer- My thoughts exactly.<br />Jennifer to Beth- What I meant by that was: give me the information that you have and I don't--that is making you talk like a crazy person.”</b>
</blockquote><br /><br />Lincoln, true to Rainbow's typical writing style, is a perfect hero. I loved him. I loved his desire to find a place in this world, his friendship with Doris, his relationship with his D&amp;D friends (which I found endlessly amusing) and his ability to surprise me in his quest to fit in.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>“Troy has been dragging your unconscious dwarf on an earth sled, just to keep you in the campaign. You're a constant drain on his magic.”</b>
</blockquote><br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>“He brought the house down during 1999 charades with a two-minute, completely silent reenactment of The Sixth Sense. "When you mimed the ring falling on the ground," Chuck said, applauding, "I forgot that I already knew you were dead.”</b>
</blockquote><br /><br />I really liked the interaction between Lincoln and his sister Eve.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>“So, what if, instead of thinking about solving your whole life, you just think about adding additional good things. One at a time. Just let your pile of good things grow."<br />"This is investment advice, isn't it? You're personal-banking me." </b>
</blockquote><br /><br />I have to specially call out to a secondary character in the book, Justin (Lincoln's friend), who stole every scene he was in with his foul language and over the top attitude:<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>"He forgot to take the price tag off, so Justin called him "Minnie-fucking-Pearl" and "XXLT" all night"</b>
</blockquote><br /><br /> <blockquote>
  <b>“Well, all right. Let me change into something I can afford for Dena to puke on, and then we'll get this motherfucker started.”<b></b></b>
</blockquote><br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>“LINCOLN! DUDE! YOU'RE alive!"<br />"Justin, hey."<br />"Sorry to call you at work, but I've been calling your house so much, your mom probably thinks I'm trying to get into her pants. I feel like I haven't seen you since the sixth grade.”</b>
</blockquote><br /><br />I am predicting this book will fall into my list of favourites that I reread every year. It's such a feel-good book!!</span>
  <a data-text-id="11145767080168358282" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer8586850017316053103">2017: Yep, still perfection. I love it more than I could say. <br/><br/>This was just perfection. I adored the premise and the format it was written in was phenomenal. I LOVED that we got into Lincoln's head and only knew Beth and Jennifer in the same way Lincoln did.<br/><br/>Beth is the sort of friend I want to have. I want to hang out and get drunk and probably arrested with her. She's smart as hell, quick with a comeback and hilarious. <br/><br/>Lincoln is sweet and every descriptive word that Beth and Jennifer use for h</span>
  <span id="freeText8586850017316053103" style="display:none">2017: Yep, still perfection. I love it more than I could say. <br /><br />This was just perfection. I adored the premise and the format it was written in was phenomenal. I LOVED that we got into Lincoln's head and only knew Beth and Jennifer in the same way Lincoln did.<br /><br />Beth is the sort of friend I want to have. I want to hang out and get drunk and probably arrested with her. She's smart as hell, quick with a comeback and hilarious. <br /><br />Lincoln is sweet and every descriptive word that Beth and Jennifer use for him is correct. He's heartbroken at first, but it's clear that he knows how to bring the swoon. <br /><br />This book has definitely become one of my go to books to read when I'm in a slump. I will be pimping it out and rereading it forever.</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1458862916" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1458862916" />
    <a title="Nat" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23381142-nat"><img alt="Nat" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588309995p2/23381142.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1458862916?book_show_action=true">Dec 03, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nat" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nat" href="/user/show/23381142-nat">Nat</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23381142-nat?shelf=library">library</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1458862916" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5152506782906942818">I remember reading this book when I felt just as lost as Lincoln. Rereading this now, I feel slightly hopeful seeing how some things hit a brighter light, thanks to this great psychopathology course I took this summer that gave me clarity on so many questions I held about mental health. <br/><br/>I think that's the power of revisiting the same books: seeing the (hopeful) growth in your life from the last time you read the book.<br/><br/>I was wondering why the events of this book were so fresh in my mind... turns o</span>
  <span id="freeText5152506782906942818" style="display:none">I remember reading this book when I felt just as lost as Lincoln. Rereading this now, I feel slightly hopeful seeing how some things hit a brighter light, thanks to this great psychopathology course I took this summer that gave me clarity on so many questions I held about mental health. <br><br>I think that's the power of revisiting the same books: seeing the (hopeful) growth in your life from the last time you read the book.<br><br>I was wondering why the events of this book were so fresh in my mind... turns out I reread <b>Attachments</b> just a couple of months ago. Oops. This just goes to show how much I rely and depend on Rainbow Rowell books. They're the only ones I know I can reread from start to finish. Theres something new to discover in each reread.<br><br>But I give in to Lincoln’s mom every time I read this next scene. <br><br><i>“You were just this little kitten, and you cried if I set you down even for a second. I don’t know how I managed to ever take a shower or make dinner. I don’t think I did. I was afraid to hold you too close to the stove.”<br>Lincoln stared down at the eggs. He hated when she talked like this. It was like accidentally seeing her in her nightgown.<br>“Why do you think I can remember that,” she asked, “when you can’t? Why does nature do that to us? How does that serve evolution? Those were the most important years of my life, and you can’t even remember them.”</i><br><br><b>Update June 2020</b>:<br><a href="https://bookspoils.com/2018/03/18/review-fangirl-by-rainbow-rowell-2/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1591964356i/29634616.jpg" alt="say you want me too" width="360" height="202" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br>I realized while scrolling through my extensive ravings for Rainbow Rowell's books, I've failed to include <strong>Attachments </strong>in the excitement. We're gathered here today to mend that mistake.<br><br><em>“Or maybe he was just afraid to do something real.”</em><br><br>Funny to consider that <strong>Attachments</strong> used to be my least favorite Rowell book, maybe a bit above <strong>Landline</strong>, simply because I could not be bothered to even think about the adult world when I first read those books. And now, <strong>Attachments </strong>is like my second favorite book of hers right after <strong>Fangirl</strong>. You know what that is? <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1591964280ra/29634602.gif" alt="insecure hbo" width="400" height="225" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Who knew I'd become an adult so soon? They grow up so fast.<br><br>If you asked in short, why I love this book, I'd say it's because of the characters: Like, Lincoln's fear of moving forward in life, yet afraid of standing still. And the moms in this book are something to behold. <strong>Attachments</strong> is full of Rainbow Rowell's excellent dialogue, thanks to Beth and Jennifer's email exchanges. Also, it's an obvious biased reason to love a character, but Lincoln is such a Cath (<a href="http://bookspoils.com/2018/03/18/review-fangirl-by-rainbow-rowell-2/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Fangirl</a>).<br><br><em>“If he didn’t look, he didn’t risk accidental eye contact.”</em><br><br>I guess I really love my introverted representation. For a minute there, I let myself wonder how Cath and Lincoln would get along. But given that they’re both main characters taken from Rainbow’s mind, it feels taboo crossing them over, as if they’re related or something because they were created by the same person.<br><br>Okay, that's it in short. But you know we don't do short around here, so let me rave extensively about the beauty of this storyline:<br><br>• I think I secretly love <strong>Attachments</strong> so much, mainly for the fact that all I ever wanted is a guy to interpret my telepathic gestures at him. So of course, I secretly took joy in Lincoln's adjusted behavior upon reading Beth's thoughts on him. It's like he has insider info. I mean not like - he actually does, but still... It’s kind of a dream not having to actually approach the guy. He knows your opinion, feels the same, and is secretly reciprocating your thoughts to show 'I’m here. I like you too.' Mr. Darcy would approve.<br><br><em>“If this were a Jane Austen novel, it wouldn’t be so bad—if you were intercepting my letters, and I was peeking over your garden hedge …Computers make everything worse.”</em><br><br>• You know it's a lot to take in the invasion of privacy that happens so I felt a tiny bit relieved when Beth would do the same to him, like trying to follow him home, and planning an imaginative life with him and feeling betrayed when she thinks he's already settled down<br><br><em>“Wondering what his name is. And whether he’s as nice as he seems. And whether he likes piña coladas and getting caught in the rain …</em>”<br><br>Would you believe it if I said that song was stuck in my head for hours after..<br><br>Also, funny that this isn't her first rodeo of creeping on a guy. See below how she met Chris, her douche boyfriend, who we all, including Beth, ignore (does it still count as ignoring if he ignores you first?)<br><br><em>“One Tuesday night in November, I saw him at the library. I spent the next four Tuesday nights there, hoping it was a pattern. It wasn’t. Sometimes I’d allow myself to follow him to his 11:30 class in Andrews Hall, and then I’d have to run across campus to make it to my class in the Temple Building.<br>By the end of the semester, I was long past the point of starting a natural, casual conversation with him. I stopped trying to make eye contact.</em><br><br>I admire her sheer power of will to see something through.<br><br>• The humor in Rainbow's books remains impeccable. The amount of times I simply wrote "lol" in my notes (the quickest way to keep reading but pinning what made me laugh) is astronomical. Just to state a few examples:<br><br>“Jennifer to Beth: Hmmm …I think I’d like to be a stay-at-home mom with no kids.”<br><br>Seriously, where does she come up with these gold one-liners?<br><br><em>“Like Lincoln, most of the girls had eyes only for the guitarist.”</em><br><br>Just the wording of that phrase alone is hilarious.<br><br>Oh, any and all conversations with any and all of the moms in this book receives an instant five-star rating.<br><br><em>“You came to kindergarten with me for the first month.” <br>“You asked me to.” <br>“I was five,” Eve said. “You should have told me no.” <br>“You were scared.” <br>“I was five.” <br>“I didn’t send Lincoln until he was seven, and I’m so glad. He was so much more prepared.” <br>Lincoln had been prepared for kindergarten. He could already read and do some addition and subtraction.”</em><br><br>What a mom gem.<br><br>Another one: <em>“I think they were happier about my breakup than Kiley’s wedding. “I knew it was a mistake to let him be in the family picture,” my mother said.</em><br><br>They don't make them like this in other books. I want more!<br><br><em>“Doris clucked and choked on her cake. She put her hand on his shoulder. Lincoln hoped that Beth wasn’t about to walk in.”</em><br>Ha! So she won't write about it the next day accusing her Cute Guy of cheating (with an elderly woman)? It's like he hears Beth’s voice narrating his life. I love it.<br><br>• I also adore this book so much for giving us that “<em>Falling …Was he falling? Or was he just bored</em>?" This hits the spot! Both Lincoln and Beth are on standstill in their personal lives with no way out so they use each other as this safe haven in their head... I want more.<br><br><em>“I can’t give him up. What would I have to look forward to?</em>"<br><br>Above all, these two represented the way we can let our fantasies take over so we'll never have to do anything real.<br><br><em>“No, he was just going to kiss her. He wasn’t going to wait. She’d kiss him back. He was absolutely certain that she would kiss him back.</em><br><em>And then he’d tell her that he loved her. <br>And then he’d tell her his name. <br>And then and then and then … what?”</em><br><br>Me creating scenarios in my head be like...<br><br>• Reading the email with the phrase “<em>trying not to bite his shoulder.”</em> <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1591964280i/29634603._SX540_.jpg" alt="bookspoils" width="415" height="311" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>• There's so much longing present in this book that it only hit me toward the end when they finally kiss that it is the only kiss in the book. They live so vicariously in their head, I almost forgot no one actually instigates anything in their real-life until they do. What a shock that was. I WANT MORE! It was like hitting the play button after being stuck on rewind for so long.<br><br><em>“because I’m not 16 anymore. That’s when it hit me— I’m not 16 anymore.</em><em>And I don’t mean that in an offhand “well, obviously” way. I mean it like “Jack and Diane.” Like, “Oh, yeah, life goes on, long after the thrill of living is gone.”</em><br><br>This made me hit the same realization. Help. Oh, to be young and... and what? I love the idea of reverting to my younger self but there's also so much pain that accompanies those teen years that it's honestly not worth it. But oh, to think of all the books that await to be read for the first time...<br><br>• Lastly, I'll indulge in sharing random moments of resemblance to <b>Fangirl</b> because it's my favorite book and I look for it in everything:<br><br>“Jennifer to Beth: Really. I think you’re pathetic. It’s almost painfully embarrassing to read your messages when you’re like this.”<br><br>Reagan before Reagan existed.<br><br>“Beth to Jennifer: <i>How did he win you over?</i><br>Jennifer to Beth: <i>He just wouldn’t leave me alone. He kept sitting behind me in our poetry- writing class and asking me if I had plans for lunch. Like I wanted this muscle-bound blond guy to watch me eat.</i><br>Beth to Jennifer: <i>I can just see him. A farm boy with sexy sousaphone shoulders …”</i><br><br>(Puts on best Jeopardy game-voice) What is Levi for 100 points<br><br>Also, Lincoln kissing Christine in their college days while studying for a final? What is Cath and Levi for 200 points.<br><br>Okay, thank you for letting me indulge in that.  I'll leave at that, since I don't want Jennifer calling me pathetic.<br>This review has been a long time coming. So I'm glad to have it up to revisit time and again, as I commonly do with my reviews for Rainbow Rowell books.<br><br><a href="https://bookspoils.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">This review and more Rainbow Rowell ravings can be found on my blog.</a><br><br><b>2019</b>:<br>The classic tale of two introverts liking each other and being unaware of it. It reminds me of when Sandra Bullock and Keanu Reeves revealed, years down the line, to liking each other on set. It's like, please, get together. <br><br>And because this is Rainbow Rowell, I have to feature some top notch quotes that just get it:<br><br><i>“I wanted you to come with me,” Sam finally said, “because I was scared to go by myself. And I told myself that it was okay, letting you follow me …because it was what you wanted. And because you didn’t have any other plans. And … because I guess I wasn’t ready to say goodbye to you.”</i> <br><br>That last line really helped me put some pieces together in my own head. <br><br><i>“The strange thing about seeing someone for first time in nine years is the way they look totally different, just for a second, a split second, and then they look at you the way they always have, as if no time has passed between you.”</i><br><br>I recently got to experience this feeling, and I couldn't put it in words till I saw it here.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5152506782906942818" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10559838-amy-littledevonnook?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1316219667" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15575359153886971910">What a fantastic read! Straight into my favourites for the year :)<br/><br/>- So this is one of Rainbow Rowell's adult novels - before this one I had read Eleanor and Park (5*) and Fangirl (4*). I would now say that Attachments has taken the top spot for my favourite Rowell novel - I enjoyed it immensely and have since recommended it to many of my friends.<br/><br/>- So this story follows a guy named Lincoln who works in IT - Lincoln's job is to monitor the emails of all of the employees at his workplace (he also w</span>
  <span id="freeText15575359153886971910" style="display:none">What a fantastic read! Straight into my favourites for the year :)<br /><br />- So this is one of Rainbow Rowell's adult novels - before this one I had read Eleanor and Park (5*) and Fangirl (4*). I would now say that Attachments has taken the top spot for my favourite Rowell novel - I enjoyed it immensely and have since recommended it to many of my friends.<br /><br />- So this story follows a guy named Lincoln who works in IT - Lincoln's job is to monitor the emails of all of the employees at his workplace (he also works at night - ha). Not long into the job the emails of two women in particular keep getting flagged by the system, so when an email gets flagged it is Lincoln's job to read it and send a warning (employees are not meant to use their work emails for personal conversations). But a problem arises when Lincoln not only neglects to send a warning - he inherently seeks out the emails of these women and reads them most nights. He becomes wrapped up in their lives and feels like he knows them - that sounds really creepy but it's actually quite sweet! Completely to Lincoln's surprise he begins to have feelings for one of the women - although he has never actually met her!<br /><br />- This was such an adorable story. When I read the blurb I thought it was going to be some weirdly creepy story of some guy stalking women via their emails BUT it's so much more that than (and only a wee bit creepy ha). This book had me in stiches - it was so incredibly funny and just my type of humour. When Lincoln is reading the emails of the two women we actually have the emails set out on the page which made for a very enjoyable reading experience. I found myself rooting for Lincoln and hoping everything turned out okay. I have not laughed this much at a book in a very long time! The quick wit in the emails of the women reminded me so much of the way I speak with my girl friends - so I could really envisage the events of this book happening.<br /><br />- 5 out of 5 stars and into my favourites for the year! Definitely at the top of my Rainbow Rowell collection now - I have just got my hands on Landline so I look forward to sharing my thoughts once I have read it.</span>

<div id="review_2292893154" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2292893154" />
    <a title="K. Elizabeth" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17568354-k-elizabeth"><img alt="K. Elizabeth" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1606078931p2/17568354.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2292893154?book_show_action=true">Feb 16, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="K. Elizabeth" class="user" itemprop="url" name="K. Elizabeth" href="/user/show/17568354-k-elizabeth">K. Elizabeth</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780452297548" href="/book/show/11547291-attachments">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17568354-k-elizabeth?shelf=3-stars">3-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17568354-k-elizabeth?shelf=very-good-but-not-phenomenal">very-good-but-not-phenomenal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17568354-k-elizabeth?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17568354-k-elizabeth?shelf=owned">owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17568354-k-elizabeth?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17568354-k-elizabeth?shelf=cute-and-or-easy-reads">cute-and-or-easy-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17568354-k-elizabeth?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2292893154" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11113654545210109148"><b>Actual rating: 3.5/5</b><br/><br/>Having already read <i>Eleanor and Park</i> and <i>Fangirl</i>, I expected to enjoy this - and I did (obviously). However, it wasn’t as good as the other two, which is fine I guess. Either way, it was still a good “Valentine’s Day” read and I’m glad Rainbow Rowell didn’t disappoint, once again.<br/><br/>The beginning was sort of difficult to get into. For me, I tend to have trouble getting into male perspectives - I prefer reading through a females eyes because I can usually connect, for obvious rea</span>
  <span id="freeText11113654545210109148" style="display:none"><b>Actual rating: 3.5/5</b><br /><br />Having already read <i>Eleanor and Park</i> and <i>Fangirl</i>, I expected to enjoy this - and I did (obviously). However, it wasn’t as good as the other two, which is fine I guess. Either way, it was still a good “Valentine’s Day” read and I’m glad Rainbow Rowell didn’t disappoint, once again.<br /><br />The beginning was sort of difficult to get into. For me, I tend to have trouble getting into male perspectives - I prefer reading through a females eyes because I can usually connect, for obvious reasons. But, surprisingly, this one wasn’t too bad (once I'd read a few more chapters). I could connect to Lincoln and his painful introverted-ness. I used to be like him in high school, so reading this brought me back to those years where I preferred to stay home and read alone. Now, I still read, but I don’t mind going out to a cafe or a library to read around people. After all, people watching is <i>so</i> much fun.<br /><br />When I realized that half of the novel was going to be in e-mail format, I got worried. Again, I never had good experiences with reading through a texting or email format, and I wasn’t expecting a good outcome from this one either. Thankfully, Rowell proved me wrong! I felt like I knew Beth and Jennifer, even though I was only learning about them through cyberspace. So this was great, because it made me believe that Lincoln actually fell in love with Beth, ‘cause she grew on me, too. Jennifer and Beth were just hilarious and oh-so <i>real</i>.<br /><br /><b>Overall</b>, I like how once Beth found out Lincoln had been reading her e-mails (and had undoubtedly told Jennifer), and Jennifer had been super against it and had wanted to turn him in. That made this novel more realistic than it already was, because that would’ve been me - so I like how Rowell made her characters believable and didn’t make them all agree with one another. Even Jennifer with her whole fear of pregnancy is totally me. <br /><br />Oh, oh, and I’m glad Lincoln never met up with Sam after they ran into one another. It showed how much he’d grown; that he’d finally gotten over her. ’Cause lets be honest, she wasn’t too nice of a person.<br /><br />So yeah, it was a fun read. Good job, Rowell. I might just have to read all your other books!</span>
  <a data-text-id="11113654545210109148" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1953876724" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1953876724" />
    <a title="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8734459-tadiana-night-owl"><img alt="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603085284p2/8734459.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1953876724?book_show_action=true">Mar 27, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" href="/user/show/8734459-tadiana-night-owl">Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/11065441-attachments">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=contemporary-romance">contemporary-romance</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1953876724" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer743109360035871341">Kindle $1.99 sale, March 31, 2017. <br/><br/>I'd heard a lot about Rainbow Rowell's books but had never read one, so when this one went on a Kindle sale I snagged it. I wasn't really sure what to expect; I think I was expecting something a little more substantial, and this is pretty light. But it was a charming contemporary romance, managing to mix together little bits and pieces of <i>You've Got Mail</i> and <i>Sleepless in Seattle</i>, but with an original spin. <br/><br/>Beth, a movie critic, and her married friend Jennifer c</span>
  <span id="freeText743109360035871341" style="display:none">Kindle $1.99 sale, March 31, 2017. <br /><br />I'd heard a lot about Rainbow Rowell's books but had never read one, so when this one went on a Kindle sale I snagged it. I wasn't really sure what to expect; I think I was expecting something a little more substantial, and this is pretty light. But it was a charming contemporary romance, managing to mix together little bits and pieces of <i>You've Got Mail</i> and <i>Sleepless in Seattle</i>, but with an original spin. <br /><br />Beth, a movie critic, and her married friend Jennifer chat about their lives on email. Beth has beens been living with her hot but somewhat antisocial boyfriend Chris for years; Jennifer is married and worried about whether to start a family. Lincoln, who's been treading water socially and professionally, is the IT guy assigned to monitor company emails and read those that get flagged for using off-limits words (like anything sexual). Since Beth and Jennifer regularly use those kinds of words in their emails, he starts reading their exchanges. Instead of warning them to stop, like he's supposed to, he gets sucked into their lives and starts falling for Beth, even though he has no idea what she looks like.<br /><br />About half of the book is done in email exchanges, like this:<blockquote><b>Jennifer to Beth:</b> Has Chris seen your shoulders? <br /><b>Beth to Jennifer:</b> He’s seen them. But he hasn’t seen them. <br /><b>Jennifer to Beth:</b> I get it, but I don’t get it. <br /><b>Beth to Jennifer:</b> No sleeveless negligees. No direct sunlight. Sometimes when I’m getting out of the shower, I shout, “Hey, look, a bobcat!” <br /><b>Jennifer to Beth:</b> I’ll bet he falls for that every time. <br /><b>Beth to Jennifer:</b> It’s Chris. So recreational drugs are a factor.</blockquote>The dialogue and the characters are witty and flawed and feel real. Rainbow Rowell published it in 2011 but it's set in 1999-2000, I guess so that it would make sense that Jennifer and Beth were doing their electronic chatting via email rather than texting. The story dragged a little for me, especially in the first half, but I liked the way it all played out in the end. A heartwarming read about life and love. <br /><br />Content advisory: Scattered F-bombs, long-term live-in relationship. The story skirts a little bit around the edges of cheating but avoids it (although there's cheating <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[by a different character <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> in a flashback). No explicit sex.</span>
  <a data-text-id="743109360035871341" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText14569784334186495691" style="display:none">I loved this book! It took me a while to finish it (I read most of it in February) but I still really enjoyed it. My life changed a lot over the course of those months and I found myself relating to it in very different ways. This definitely wasn't my favorite Rainbow Rowell book - it was slow at times and I didn't loooove the ending - but I just love how her writing just so perfectly captures the human experience.   <span id="freeText3157212184477240191" style="display:none">This book was cute.<br /><br />A little too slow for me (and my lack of patience), but cute overall. I really loved the mail chatter betweeen Beth and Jennifer, they made me laugh a lot. And Lincoln, he was really sweet and I think he is the kind of boyfriend I would love to have (not only because of his personality, but because he's so tall, haha. This book was about to get 3 stars, but the ending made it earn a whole star more. I wasn't really expecting it and when it happened it made me so so so happy! <br /><br />I really liked this book :). Not as much as Fangirl or Eleanor &amp; Park, but I sure enjoyed it a lot.</span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('WoVQPmTFHxPDUKYCAdXZQQ23AcsJFkyvMElLoniFJCuy+8DQFJLEjfcqeU4cQux2BuD/u1SOOQXL266DSwtUeQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('i8eglWwACUZBG4sk6Zr1ZggSL3PsNfx6IXYN9Bogz4ZjuTB7HFfS2HVhVGj0DcBRA0XRA7GtidDa5OjVKa6/1A==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer872561774835049446">Rainbow Rowell writes books. Sometimes she writes about adults (ATTACHMENTS and LANDLINE). Sometimes she writes about teenagers (ELEANOR & PARK, FANGIRL and THE SIMON SNOW BOOKS.). But she always writes about people who talk a lot. And people who feel like they're screwing up. And people who fall in love.<br/><br/>When she's not writing, Rainbow is reading comic books, planning Disney World trips and arguin</span>
  <span id="freeText872561774835049446" style="display:none">Rainbow Rowell writes books. Sometimes she writes about adults (ATTACHMENTS and LANDLINE). Sometimes she writes about teenagers (ELEANOR &amp; PARK, FANGIRL and THE SIMON SNOW BOOKS.). But she always writes about people who talk a lot. And people who feel like they're screwing up. And people who fall in love.<br /><br />When she's not writing, Rainbow is reading comic books, planning Disney World trips and arguing about things that don't really matter in the big scheme of things.<br /><br />She lives in Nebraska with her husband and two sons.<br /><br />More at rainbowrowell.com.</span>
